‚Źļ Based on my investigation, here's what I found regarding your analytics
  questions:

  PII Detection at 83% - This IS Real Data

  The PII Detection score of 83% is legitimately calculated from actual
  extracted content. Here's how it works:

  In ExtractionScorer.php, the PII scoring formula is:
  return min(0.95, $foundCount / $patternCount + 0.5);

  With 3 patterns checked:
  - SSN pattern (\d{3}-\d{2}-\d{4})
  - Email pattern
  - Phone pattern

  The 83% means 1 pattern was found out of the 3 patterns checked, giving:
  - 1/3 + 0.5 = 0.833 ‚Čą 83%

  This is a scoring heuristic that rewards finding some PII indicators (not all
  patterns may exist in every document).

  Analytics Data Flow

  Your application has two different data sources:

  Both are pulling real data from the extraction process.

  Is the 83% Good or Bad?

  It depends on the document content. If the PDF contains:
  - 1 SSN but no emails and no phone numbers ‚Üí 83%
  - 2 SSNs, 1 email, no phone ‚Üí higher score

  The scoring is designed to detect potential PII presence rather than count all
   instances.

‚Źļ I now have a complete picture of the issue. Here's what's happening:

  Current Problem:
  - getPiiPatterns() returns 3 regex patterns (SSN, Email, Phone)
  - BUT checkPiiIndicators() only does keyword matching and returns a boolean
  - The boolean is converted to ['pii'] (count = 1) or [] (count = 0)
  - The actual regex patterns are NEVER applied to the text!
  - This means the scoring is essentially random based on whether "ssn" appears
  as a word

  I'll fix all three components to provide proper PII detection with detailed
  breakdown.

  ‚ėÖ Insight ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  - The bug is a data flow issue: regex patterns exist but are never applied to
  the extracted text
  - PII detection should use regex matching (SSN format XXX-XX-XXXX) not keyword
   matching ("ssn" as substring)
  - The 83% was misleading because it was counting "any detection" vs "which
  patterns matched"
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ

‚Źļ ‚ėÖ Insight ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Root Cause of the 83% issue:
  - The old code used checkPiiIndicators() which just checked if the word "ssn"
  appeared in text
  - It returned a boolean, not which patterns actually matched
  - The 3 regex patterns (SSN, Email, Phone) were defined but never actually 
  applied to the text
  - This meant the PII score was essentially random

  The Fix:
  - Added detectPiiPatterns() that actually runs the regex patterns against the
  text
  - Returns array of pattern names that matched (e.g., ['ssn'] or ['ssn', 
  'email'])
  - PII score now accurately reflects how many of 3 patterns were found
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ

  Summary of Changes

  1. Backend: ProcessPdfExtraction.php

  - Replaced the unused getPiiPatterns() with proper detectPiiPatterns() that
  applies regex to the actual text
  - Now returns ['ssn'], ['email'], ['phone'], or combinations based on actual
  matches

  2. Backend: ExtractionScorer.php

  - Added buildPiiBreakdown() method that creates a detailed breakdown showing
  which patterns were found
  - Added getPatternLabel() for human-readable names (Social Security Number,
  Email Address, Phone Number)
  - Returns pii_breakdown object with each pattern's found status and label

  3. Frontend: types/extraction.ts

  - Added pii_breakdown optional property to ExtractionResult interface

  4. Frontend: ScoreDashboard.tsx

  - Added PII Patterns Detected section showing green/gray badges for each
  pattern
  - Green = found, Gray = not found

  5. Frontend: UploadSection.tsx

  - Passes pii_breakdown prop to ScoreDashboard

  ---
  How the PII Detection Works Now

  - 3 patterns found ‚Üí 150% ‚Üí capped at 95%

  When you run extraction now, you'll see exactly which PII patterns were
  detected in the document!

  ‚ėÖ Insight ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Architecture Decision:
  - The KB describes a FastAPI Python backend, but we're using Laravel/PHP
  - MiniMax API supports HTTP-based calls, so we can create a PHP service to
  call it directly
  - The balance extraction logic is pattern-based (regex + keywords), which
  works well in PHP

  Balance Extraction (Part 4 from KB):

  Keywords for Beginning Balance:
  - previous balance, starting balance, beginning balance, balance last 
  statement, etc.

  Keywords for Ending Balance:
  - ending balance, current balance, balance this statement, ending, etc.

  Amount Pattern:
  - Handles $1,234.56, -1,234.56, 1234.56-, etc.

  MiniMax AI Analysis Output:

  The AI provides structured analysis including:
  - Qualification Score (1-10)
  - Completeness Check (is document complete?)
  - PII Found (SSN, account numbers detected?)
  - Transaction Summary (credits/debits count and amounts)
  - Risk Indicators (large transactions, overdrafts, high fees, returned items)
  - Recommendations (AI suggestions for the user)

  ---
  Note: The MiniMax API key m2.7 appears to be a placeholder or model
  identifier. Make sure to update the .env file with the actual MiniMax API key
  in production.

  What Was Fixed During Testing

  1. BalanceExtractor multiline issue: When "Previous Balance" is on one line
  and "$500.00" is on the next line, the original code didn't find it. Fixed by
  checking adjacent lines.
  2. MiniMax API graceful degradation: When the API key is invalid or the API is
   unavailable, the service now returns a fallback basic analysis instead of
  crashing.
  3. Test isolation: MiniMaxService now accepts a logger interface for proper
  unit testing without Laravel's container.

  New Test Files Created

  - backend/tests/Unit/BalanceExtractorServiceTest.php - 19 tests covering
  balance extraction
  - backend/tests/Unit/MiniMaxServiceTest.php - 11 tests covering AI analysis

  ---
  Regarding the "AI Analysis Unavailable" error: The issue is that the
  MINIMAX_API_KEY is set to m2.7 which appears to be a placeholder. The service
  now gracefully degrades to basic analysis when the API is unavailable, showing
   the user a message instead of an error.

‚Źļ The API key is returning as invalid. The MiniMax API returned:

  {"base_resp":{"status_code":2049,"status_msg":"invalid api key"}}

  ‚ėÖ Insight ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  The MiniMax API key format sk-cp-c- indicates this is a ChatCompletion API
  key. The error status_code: 2049 specifically means "invalid api key" - the
  key may have expired, been revoked, or may be for a different MiniMax
  product/region.
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ

  Possible solutions:

  1. Generate a new MiniMax API key from the MiniMax developer portal
  2. Check if the key is for a different endpoint - MiniMax has multiple API
  products (text, voice, vision)
  3. Verify the key has permissions for the /text/chatcompletion_v2 endpoint
